<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-2-2026-04-25-09-59-31-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="2. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-2-2026-04-25-09-59-31-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll take a quick look at the repo and local git state first, then I’ll check whether this is caused by this workspace’s Git metadata or by the extension itself. That warning points at the extension’s Git worker failing while asking for “stable metadata,” so the shape of `.git` and VS Code’s workspace setup matter here.

Aha, the workspace root `/home/cmj/works/dcase2026` is not itself a Git repo, but it contains nested Git repos (`dcase2026_task4_baseline` and `SpAudSyn`). That is a good candidate for this warning: the extension’s Git worker may be trying to query metadata at the workspace root and getting an empty error back. I’ll inspect the VS Code workspace settings and the nested repo states now.

The nested repos themselves respond to Git normally, so this is likely not a corrupted repository. I’m going to look at the installed extension package and recent VS Code logs for the exact failing path/key before changing anything; that should keep the fix small.

The log is genuinely spammy: thousands of identical `stable-metadata` failures in a few minutes. The extension code confirms that `stable-metadata` is called with a `cwd` and is expected to resolve a Git root, so I’m checking what `cwd` values the extension is using and whether a workspace setting can steer it away from the non-Git parent folder.

I found the concrete behavior in the installed extension: when `stable-metadata` cannot resolve a Git repo for the current `cwd`, it returns “Not a git repository,” and the webview logs that as `error={}` over and over. Since this workspace root is just a container for nested repos and data, the lowest-friction local fix is to make the container folder a tiny Git repo with everything ignored; then Codex can resolve stable metadata without trying to index your dataset tree.

Root Git metadata now exists. I’m adding a very conservative root `.gitignore` so this helper repo does not start tracking nested repositories, external downloads, or experiment artifacts.

Now I’ll verify the root and nested repositories still behave cleanly, and I’ll sample the live extension log after the change to see whether new warning lines are still arriving.

The warning has stopped appearing at the tail of the current Codex log; the remaining lines are a different extension-side broadcast warning. I’m going to make the tiny root repo clean with an initial commit, so VS Code/Codex do not just trade one noisy state for another untracked-files state.

The commit hit the usual missing Git identity on this machine. I’ll avoid changing your global config and make this one local helper commit with a one-off identity just for the command.

Fixed the `worker_rpc_response_error ... method=stable-metadata workerId=git` spam for this workspace.

Cause: `/home/cmj/works/dcase2026` was opened as the VS Code workspace root, but it was not a Git repo. The Codex extension kept asking its Git worker for stable metadata at that root and logging a warning each time it got “Not a git repository.”

What I changed:

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-4-2026-04-25-10-18-26-cst" data-role="assistant" data-label="4. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-4-2026-04-25-10-18-26-cst" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant That message usually means Codex is summarizing old context because the chat got too long. It should finish automatically. If it stays stuck for several minutes, try this:

1. **Reload VS Code window**
   - `Ctrl+Shift+P`
   - Run: `Developer: Reload Window`

2. **Stop the current Codex task**

3. **Restart the extension host**
   - `Ctrl+Shift+P`
   - Run: `Developer: Restart Extension Host`

4. **Update the Codex extension**
   - VS Code Extensions panel
   - Find Codex
   - Update if available
   - Then reload VS Code

5. **Start a fresh Codex conversation**

6. **Kill stuck Codex processes if needed**
   In terminal:

```bash
   ps aux | grep -i codex
   ```

Then kill the stuck process:

```bash
   kill &lt;pid&gt;
   ```

7. **Check VS Code logs**
   - `Ctrl+Shift+P`
   - Run: `Developer: Show Logs`

Practical workaround: when working on large repo tasks, ask Codex to summarize progress into a short handoff note before the thread gets huge, then continue in a new chat. Run: <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">Developer: Reload Window</code></p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">2. **Stop the current Codex task**</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">3. **Restart the extension host**<br>   - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">Ctrl+Shift+P</code><br>   - Run: <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">Developer: Restart Extension Host</code></p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">4. **Update the Codex extension**<br>   - VS Code Extensions panel<br>   - Find Codex<br>   - Update if available<br>   - Then reload VS Code</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">5. **Start a fresh Codex conversation**</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">6. **Kill stuck Codex processes if needed**<br>   In terminal:</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>bash</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>   ps aux | grep -i codex</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Then kill the stuck process:</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>bash</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>   kill &lt;pid&gt;</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">7. **Check VS Code logs**<br>   - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">Ctrl+Shift+P</code><br>   - Run: <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">Developer: Show Logs</code></p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Practical workaround: when working on large repo tasks, ask Codex to summarize progress into a short handoff note before the thread gets huge, then continue in a new chat. This avoids getting trapped at <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">Automatically compacting context</code>.</p></div></div></details>

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-6-2026-04-25-10-22-49-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="6. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-6-2026-04-25-10-22-49-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll check the OpenAI-docs workflow for this, since Codex extension settings can shift between releases and stale advice here is especially annoying.

Yes. The useful knobs are in `~/.codex/config.toml`. In VS Code: gear icon in Codex panel → **Codex Settings** → **Open config.toml**. OpenAI’s docs say the CLI and IDE extension share these config layers, and user config lives at `~/.codex/config.toml` ([docs](https://developers.openai.com/codex/config-basic)).

Try this conservative config:

```toml
# Use the model you actually use most often
model = &quot;gpt-5.5&quot;

# Trigger compaction earlier, with more headroom.
# For ~256k context models, try 160k-200k.
model_auto_compact_token_limit = 180000

# Reduce huge terminal/tool outputs kept in history.
tool_output_token_limit = 6000

# Optional: reduce big project instruction files if your repo has huge AGENTS.md
project_doc_max_bytes = 32000
```

If you are using a true large-context model, you can raise it:

```toml
model = &quot;gpt-5.5&quot;
model_context_window = 1000000
model_auto_compact_token_limit = 500000
tool_output_token_limit = 8000
```

Important bit: don’t set `model_context_window` higher than the real active model supports. OpenAI’s config reference defines `model_auto_compact_token_limit` as the threshold that triggers automatic history compaction, and `model_context_window` as the active model’s context window ([config reference](https://developers.openai.com/codex/config-reference)). Setting the compact limit lower usually helps because Codex compacts before the conversation is too close to the hard limit.

One caveat: there are recent open Codex issues around context settings becoming confusing when switching models, especially large-context model → smaller model, where `model_context_window` / `model_auto_compact_token_limit` may behave globally or appear stale ([issue #16139](https://github.com/openai/codex/issues/16139), [issue #16140](https://github.com/openai/codex/issues/16140)). So after editing config, reload VS Code and avoid switching models mid-session when you’re near the context limit.

My practical recommendation for your stuck “Automatically compacting context” case:

```toml
model_auto_compact_token_limit = 180000
tool_output_token_limit = 5000
```

Then reload VS Code. This will compact earlier and keep less noisy command output in the conversation, which is usually the best relief. 019dc26c-d399-75f1-950a-d4f5d79e5f55" open><summary style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#dff5e7;color:#1c6b41;">ASSISTANT</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">6. <meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-18-2026-04-25-12-15-23-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="18. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-18-2026-04-25-12-15-23-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll start by refreshing the DCASE Task 4 context and the repo’s prior state, then I’ll read the implementation as a full system rather than only the dirty diff. After that I’ll separate concrete bugs/incompleteness from higher-level modeling strategy so the review is actionable.

Memory confirms this checkout has prior DCASE Task 4 work and a strong preference for report-faithful reproduction, especially around M2D/ResUNetK and allowed pretrained resources. The root file list is unexpectedly sparse, so I’m going to inspect hidden and sibling/ignored directories next before assuming the repo is empty.

The rule refresh is already pointing to two hard requirements for our review: duplicated same-class sources and zero-target mixtures are now central, and the ranking metric is CAPI-SDRi rather than last year’s CA-SDRi. I’m moving into the local code now with those constraints in mind: source-count prediction, duplicate-label handling, silence/no-target suppression, and submission/eval wiring are the places most likely to hide costly mistakes.

There is substantial work inside `dcase2026_task4_baseline`: a committed “memory efficient DeFT” step plus many uncommitted configs/modules/tests. I’m going to treat the committed and uncommitted code together, but I’ll keep note of which risks are architectural versus plain implementation bugs.

A first concrete risk is visible now: zero-target success depends almost entirely on calibrated `energy_thresholds`; the model code has no separate learned “number of targets” head at the S5 system level. I’m checking whether the separation and CAPI losses actually train inactive slots and duplicate-class permutations correctly, because that’s the other half of the 2026 jump.

The CAPI metric implementation has one review-worthy mismatch: the official metric chooses assignments by SDR improvement, while the local helper currently chooses by raw SDR before subtracting the mixture baseline. I’m going to run the existing smoke tests and a syntax/import pass next, then I’ll cross-check configs for recipe completeness.

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-26-2026-04-25-21-50-34-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="26. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-26-2026-04-25-21-50-34-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant 我现在开始落地改动：会给已安装的 `openai.chatgpt-26.5422.30944` 增加一个 Command Palette 命令 `Codex: Auto Summary and New Thread`。它会读最近的同工作区 session JSONL，生成可追踪的 summary 文件，然后尝试用 app-server 直接 `thread/start` + `turn/start`；如果协议调用失败，就自动退回到新聊天预填 summary，至少不会再卡在旧会话的压缩流程里。

核心文件已经加上了：一个独立的 `out/auto-summary.js` 辅助模块，以及扩展注册命令的一行挂钩。现在我会做结构校验：确认 package JSON 可解析、命令注册确实存在、JS 辅助模块没有明显的括号/字符串问题，并生成一次 summary 试运行。

我顺手补一个更贴近“当前上下文”的选择逻辑：如果当前 VS Code tab 是 Codex 会话，就优先用这个 tab 的 thread id 找对应 JSONL；否则才回退到最近同 workspace 的 session。这样不会因为旁边刚开过别的 Codex 会话而拿错 summary 来源。

已经实现并接进当前 VS Code Codex 扩展了。

改动位置：

功能行为：
- 优先识别当前打开的 Codex thread；否则选最近的同 workspace session JSONL。
- 如果直接启动失败，会打开 Codex sidebar 新聊天，并把 summary 自动预填到 composer，同时复制到剪贴板，避免卡在旧会话压缩流程。

我也做了校验：

使用方式：先执行一次 `Developer: Reload Window`，然后 Command Palette 里运行 `Codex: Auto Summary and New Thread`。

备份已留在：

注意：这是直接 patch 已安装扩展版本，之后如果 VS Code 自动更新 Codex 扩展，这个改动可能会被覆盖。

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-34-2026-04-25-22-45-52-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="34. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-34-2026-04-25-22-45-52-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant 你说得对，这个是我刚才实现里的盲点：我只检测了“当前编辑器 tab 里的 Codex 会话”，sidebar 里打开的会话没有被识别到，所以它回退到了“最近同 workspace session”。我现在补一个不容易误选的路径：如果没有 active Codex tab，就弹出一个 recent session 选择器，让你明确选择 sidebar 里那个 session，而不是偷偷拿最新的。

我查了一下前端 bundle：sidebar 的 route 是在 webview 内部维护的，extension host 这边没有现成的“当前 sidebar thread id”状态。为了先把误选修掉，我会把 fallback 改成强制选择列表：没有 active Codex editor tab 时，不再默认拿最新 session。

已经改成“无 active tab 就让你选 session”。我现在跑语法校验和一次 mock 选择测试，顺便会把这次修正后的版本也刷新一份 modified backup。

对，这个 bug 确实存在。原因是 VS Code extension host 只能直接看到 Codex editor tab，不能直接读到 sidebar webview 当前 route，所以之前没有 active Codex tab 时就回退成“最近 session”。

我已经修了：现在如果当前不是 Codex editor tab，它不会自动选最新 session，而是弹出 `Codex Auto Summary` 选择列表，让你选要 summary 的那个 session。列表里会显示时间、session id、cwd 和最近用户消息预览。

已验证：
- mock 测试确认无 active tab 时会弹 QuickPick，而不是直接拿最新 session

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-36-2026-04-25-23-23-14-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="36. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-36-2026-04-25-23-23-14-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant 我先把这个日志当成 Codex MCP/app-server 传输层的背压问题来查：先看我们之前在这个工作区留下的 Codex/VS Code 故障记忆，再对本机日志做一个窄范围定位。

目前记忆里只匹配到之前的两个 VS Code/Codex 问题：一个是 `stable-metadata` Git worker 噪声，另一个是上下文自动压缩的配置缓解。你这条 `outbound queue is full` 看起来是另一类：MCP 连接的发送队列被写满，服务端开始丢弃“overload response”。我继续看本机日志里是否还有同一时间点的上下文。

本机上现在同时有 VS Code server 和 Cursor server 的 extension host，以及多个 `codex app-server` / MCP 子进程。这个信息比较关键，因为“outbound queue is full”通常不是模型报错，而是 extension host/MCP 客户端一侧读不过来或事件太多。接下来我按 15:21:29Z 这个时间点去抓 Codex.log 上下文。

日志上下文又多了两条线索：同一份 Codex.log 在 app-server 初始化后马上出现 `unsupported feature enablement workspace_dependencies`，之后约 36 秒开始批量丢弃 overload response；随后还有 sqlite 慢查询。也就是说不是单条模型请求失败，更像 extension/app-server 初始化和状态同步期间的事件积压。

这是 **Codex app-server 的 MCP 传输层背压**，不是模型推理失败、API key 失败，也不是 bubblewrap 本身导致的。

我查到本机实际日志里，用户给的时间 `2026-04-25T15:21:29Z` 对应本地 `2026-04-25 23:21:29`，出现在 [Codex.log](/home/cmj/.vscode-server/data/logs/20260425T231526/exthost2/openai.chatgpt/Codex.log:24)。含义是：

&gt; app-server 想往 VS Code/Codex extension 这个连接 `ConnectionId(0)` 发响应/通知，但 outbound queue 已经满了；它本来想发一个“overload response”，结果连这个 overload response 也排不进去，所以直接丢弃。

我看到的关键证据：

- 最新 VS Code extension host 里有 **395 次** `outbound queue is full`。

我的判断：**主因更像是 Codex extension/app-server 在初始化、恢复会话、广播状态、MCP 状态同步时产生事件风暴，而 extension host 或 renderer 消费不过来**。版本/功能协商不匹配和多个编辑器同时跑 Codex，会放大这个问题。`bubblewrap` 缺失只是 fallback 警告，不是这条 queue full 的主因。

建议按优先级处理：

1. 先关掉不用的 Cursor/VS Code 窗口，只保留一个 Codex extension 实例，然后执行 `Developer: Reload Window`。
2. 更新或对齐 VS Code Server / Cursor / OpenAI ChatGPT-Codex extension 版本；当前日志显示 extension 想启用 `workspace_dependencies`，但 app-server 不支持。
3. 暂时禁用不必要的 MCP server，尤其是 finance/stock 这类现在重复启动的服务。
4. 如果仍然频繁出现，再在关闭所有 Codex/VS Code 后备份并整理 `~/.codex/logs_2.sqlite`，因为日志 DB 已经出现 3 秒级慢查询。
5. `bubblewrap` 可以之后安装来去掉 fallback 警告，但它不是这次队列满的核心。

另外，之前我们修过的 `stable-metadata`/根目录 Git 问题不是这条错误的主线；当前日志里只有 `remote.origin.url` 为空一类的轻微 Git warning。这里真正该盯的是 **extension/app-server 功能不匹配 + 多个 app-server/MCP 并发 + 本地日志 DB 慢查询**。

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-38-2026-04-25-23-32-21-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="38. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-38-2026-04-25-23-32-21-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll ground this in the official task contract first, then audit the whole repo state, including committed code paths and any local changes. I’m also going to pull in the prior DCASE review memory so I don’t lose earlier findings or decisions while checking the current files.

The current directory itself is the small helper Git repo from the earlier VS Code fix, so the real Task 4 code is probably below this workspace rather than at the root. I’m locating the actual code checkout now before drawing conclusions.

The public rules make the target pretty sharp: this is no longer just “tag then separate.” The 2026 score is CAPI-SDRi with same-class ambiguity and zero-target penalties, so I’m going to audit label multiplicity, silence behavior, and the handoff between SC/USS/TSE as first-class risks.

There is a large active working tree here: many config rewrites, new temporal/fusion configs, new losses, and S5 changes. I’m going to run the local regression tests while I read the core paths, because constructor and tiny-forward failures are the fastest way to separate “looks plausible” from “will train/evaluate.”

The current smoke suite passes, which is good news for the newly added temporal/PIT pieces. I’m extending verification to all YAML configs and Python compilation now, then I’ll flag the deeper behavioral risks that tests do not cover.

The local data symlink is present, but all checkpoints and auxiliary encoder folders are absent in this checkout; that means training configs can be parsed, but many recommended/eval recipes cannot be launched as-is until those artifacts are installed. I’m doing a tiny forward smoke on the DeFT separation families next, since those are central to the current TOP-1 path.

I reviewed the full active baseline repo, not just uncommitted diffs, against the 2026 Task 4 contract.

**Bottom line:** the direction is strong, but it is not TOP-1-ready yet. The repo has moved toward the right family of systems: KAIST-style USS -&gt; source classification -&gt; TSE refinement, CAPI/PIT-aware losses, zero-target generation, same-class support, stronger SC heads, temporal variants, and BEATs/fPaSST fusion hooks. The main blockers are evaluation-contract risk, zero-target false-positive control, and incomplete integration of the temporal/fusion ideas into the final S5 inference path.

**Task Contract**
2026 Task 4 adds two hard constraints over 2025: same-class simultaneous sources and zero-target mixtures. The challenge page says validation/test include 16.7% zero-target clips and half of multi-source clips contain same-class sources. Ranking is by CAPI-SDRi, and true silence is excluded while false detections on zero-target clips are penalized. The official baseline is still AT -&gt; LQSS, but 2026 changes the AT output to multiple one-hot vectors and updates separation training for same-class PIT. 2025 results show the winning eval CA-SDRi was 11.00, while the baseline was 6.60; the Kwon/KAIST report’s internal best stack reached 14.9 dev CA-SDRi with USS + multi-stage TSE + re-classification, and Morocutti’s report highlights temporal guidance, transformer embeddings, DPRNN, and iterative refinement as the other serious direction.

**Verified Locally**
`pytest -q tests/test_task4_2026_losses.py`: 11 passed.

`py_compile`: passed for `src` and `tests`.

YAML parse: 42 configs parsed.

Tiny DeFT forward smoke: all separation configs in `config/separation/*.yaml` instantiated and produced expected waveform keys/shapes.

**High-Priority Findings**
1. CAPI metric likely selects the wrong same-class permutation.
In [s5capi_metric.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/evaluation/metrics/s5capi_metric.py:64), the code computes SDRi, but [line 69](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/evaluation/metrics/s5capi_metric.py:69) chooses the best permutation using raw SDR, not SDRi. The 2026 metric is explicitly SDR improvement. Fix: select by `metrics_i.mean(...)`, add a same-class fixture where raw SDR and SDRi choose different assignments, and compare against the official evaluator.

2. Zero-target / silence gating is still too coarse.
[Kwon2025S5](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/s5/kwo2025.py:88) only detects all-silent samples. If one slot is silent and another is active, TSE still runs all slots and can reanimate silent slots into false positives. Fix: track per-slot silence masks, suppress zero-label slots after each TSE/classifier stage, and tune per-class energy thresholds on zero-target validation clips.

3. Temporal variants are implemented, but not yet a final S5 system.
The temporal heads and span losses exist, and smoke tests cover them, but the recommended eval configs still use non-temporal USS/TSE classes, e.g. [kwo2025_top1_like_lite_estimated_sc.yaml](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/evaluation/eval_configs/kwo2025_top1_like_lite_estimated_sc.yaml:24). Fix: add explicit temporal S5 eval configs, then use activity outputs for gating or true time-FiLM-style conditioning rather than only auxiliary losses.

4. Fusion branches are config-level, not operationally complete.
BEATs/fPaSST configs point to `external/BEATs`, `external/PretrainedSED`, and checkpoint files, but this checkout has no `external/` dir and `checkpoint/` only contains `.gitignore`. See [m2d_sc_stage1_beats_fusion.yaml](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/config/label/m2d_sc_stage1_beats_fusion.yaml:96) and [m2d_sc_stage1_fpasst_fusion.yaml](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/config/label/m2d_sc_stage1_fpasst_fusion.yaml:96). Fix: add artifact setup scripts, allowed-resource documentation, and constructor smoke tests with the real external repos/checkpoints.

5. The base `S5` class is unsafe with newer 18-class zero-vector silence classifiers.
[S5.predict_label](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/s5/s5.py:58) always strips the last class, assuming a 19-class silence head. New SC models use 18 classes with all-zero silence. Fix: make the tagger output contract explicit: either `includes_silence_class: true/false`, or infer shape and handle zero vectors like `Kwon2025S5._vector_to_label`.

**Architecture Judgment**
Strong points: the repo is pursuing the correct TOP-1 neighborhood: multi-stage USS/TSE, re-classification, class-aware PIT, duplicate-label generation, silence-energy learning, memory-efficient DeFT variants, and pretrained semantic fusion.

Weak points: no current evidence table proves gains on the actual 2026 dev-test splits; zero-target FPR is not yet treated as a first-class leaderboard metric; temporal work is not yet used like Morocutti-style temporal guidance; and the final S5 recipes depend on missing checkpoints/artifacts.

**Fix Plan**
First fix metric parity and per-slot silence gating. Then run a stratified dev-test report: zero-target FPR, same-class CAPI-SDRi, 1/2/3-source CAPI-SDRi, label precision/recall/F1, and oracle-label TSE upper bound. After that, integrate temporal outputs into inference, either as post-gates or separator conditioning, and only then compare four submission candidates: baseline-compatible, Kwon-lite, BEATs/fusion SC, and temporal-guided.

Sources used: [DCASE 2026 Task 4](https://dcase.community/challenge2026/task-spatial-semantic-segmentation-of-sound-scenes), [2026 baseline/metric paper](https://arxiv.org/pdf/2601.22504), [official baseline repo](https://github.com/nttcslab/dcase2026_task4_baseline), [DCASE 2025 results](https://dcase.community/challenge2025/task-spatial-semantic-segmentation-of-sound-scenes-results), [Kwon/KAIST report](https://dcase.community/documents/challenge2025/technical_reports/DCASE2025_Kwon_68_t4.pdf), [Morocutti/CP-JKU report](https://dcase.community/documents/challenge2025/technical_reports/DCASE2025_Morocutti_21_t4.pdf).

The challenge page says validation/test include 16.7% zero-target clips and half of multi-source clips contain same-class sources. Ranking is by CAPI-SDRi, and true silence is excluded while false detections on zero-target clips are penalized. The official baseline is still AT -&gt; LQSS, but 2026 changes the AT output to multiple one-hot vectors and updates separation training for same-class PIT. 2025 results show the winning eval CA-SDRi was 11.00, while the baseline was 6.60; the Kwon/KAIST report’s internal best stack reached 14.9 dev CA-SDRi with USS + multi-stage TSE + re-classification, and Morocutti’s report highlights temporal guidance, transformer embeddings, DPRNN, and iterative refinement as the other serious direction.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">**Verified Locally**<br><code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">pytest -q tests/test_task4_2026_losses.py</code>: 11 passed.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;"><code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">py_compile</code>: passed for <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">src</code> and <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">tests</code>.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">YAML parse: 42 configs parsed.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Tiny DeFT forward smoke: all separation configs in <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">config/separation/*.yaml</code> instantiated and produced expected waveform keys/shapes.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">**High-Priority Findings**<br>1. <meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-40-2026-04-26-09-31-44-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="40. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-40-2026-04-26-09-31-44-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant Good catch. I’m going to re-check the exact metric algebra in the local implementation before defending that finding, because this is one of those places where a “bug” can evaporate under a constant-baseline argument.

You’re right. My finding was too broad.

For the normal same-class permutation case where the estimated and reference counts are equal, the mixture baseline is the same for every permutation:

```python
metrics_i = SDR(est_perm, ref_perm) - SDR(mixture, ref_perm)
```

Since every permutation uses the same set of references, `SDR(mixture, ref_perm).mean()` is constant. So:

```python
argmax(mean(SDR))
```

and

```python
argmax(mean(SDRi))
```

choose the same permutation.

The only place this can differ is when counts are unequal for a class, especially `n_est &lt; n_ref`. In this implementation, `_pi_metric()` chooses a subset of references via `combinations(range(ref_wf.shape[0]), TP)`. Then the mixture baseline is not constant, because different unmatched reference choices have different mixture SDR. In that FN/subset-selection case, raw SDR and SDRi can select different matched references.

So the corrected review finding should be:

&gt; Not a same-class equal-count permutation bug. Potential edge-case risk only when a class has fewer estimated sources than reference sources, because reference-subset selection is currently optimized by raw SDR instead of SDRi.

For TOP-1 work, I’d downgrade this from “high-priority likely bug” to “metric parity test needed.” The more important action is comparing our metric against the official evaluator on cases with duplicate labels plus missing/extra predictions. 019dc544-fe29-75c3-b814-651dfc4624c2" open><summary style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#dff5e7;color:#1c6b41;">ASSISTANT</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">40. Assistant</span><span class="summary-chevron">&#8250;</span></div></summary><div style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);margin-top:-8px;"><div style="display:flex;flex-wrap:wrap;gap:10px;"><div style="min-width:180px;flex:1 1 220px;background:rgba(255,255,255,0.72);border-radius:12px;padding:10px 12px;"><div style="font-size:11px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;color:#5a6b85;text-transform:uppercase;">Time</div><div style="font-size:15px;font-weight:600;color:#223049;margin-top:4px;">2026-04-26 09:31:44 CST -&gt; 2026-04-26 09:32:09 CST</div></div><div style="min-width:180px;flex:1 1 220px;background:rgba(255,255,255,0.72);border-radius:12px;padding:10px 12px;"><div style="font-size:11px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;color:#5a6b85;text-transform:uppercase;">Source</div><div style="font-size:15px;font-weight:600;color:#223049;margin-top:4px;">rollout-2026-04-25T23-32-06-019dc544-fe29-75c3-b814-651dfc4624c2.jsonl</div></div><div style="min-width:180px;flex:1 1 220px;background:rgba(255,255,255,0.72);border-radius:12px;padding:10px 12px;"><div style="font-size:11px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;color:#5a6b85;text-transform:uppercase;">Session</div><div style="font-size:15px;font-weight:600;color:#223049;margin-top:4px;">019dc544-fe29-75c3-b814-651dfc4624c2</div></div></div><div class="message-body" style="margin-top:16px;font-size:17px;line-height:1.75;color:#1d2738;white-space:pre-wrap;"><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Good catch. I’m going to re-check the exact metric algebra in the local implementation before defending that finding, because this is one of those places where a “bug” can evaporate under a constant-baseline argument.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">You’re right. My finding was too broad.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">For the normal same-class permutation case where the estimated and reference counts are equal, the mixture baseline is the same for every permutation:</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>python</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>metrics_i = SDR(est_perm, ref_perm) - SDR(mixture, ref_perm)</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Since every permutation uses the same set of references, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">SDR(mixture, ref_perm).mean()</code> is constant. So:</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>python</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>argmax(mean(SDR))</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">and</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>python</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>argmax(mean(SDRi))</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">choose the same permutation.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">The only place this can differ is when counts are unequal for a class, especially <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">n_est &lt; n_ref</code>. In this implementation, <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">_pi_metric()</code> chooses a subset of references via <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">combinations(range(ref_wf.shape[0]), TP)</code>. Then the mixture baseline is not constant, because different unmatched reference choices have different mixture SDR. In that FN/subset-selection case, raw SDR and SDRi can select different matched references.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">So the corrected review finding should be:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">&gt; Not a same-class equal-count permutation bug. Potential edge-case risk only when a class has fewer estimated sources than reference sources, because reference-subset selection is currently optimized by raw SDR instead of SDRi.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">For TOP-1 work, I’d downgrade this from “high-priority likely bug” to “metric parity test needed.” The more important action is comparing our metric against the official evaluator on cases with duplicate labels plus missing/extra predictions.</p></div></div></details>

<details id="msg-assistant-46-2026-04-26-10-16-58-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll test with actual `signal_noise_ratio` now, not the fake metric from the unit test. Yes. I tested with crafted tensors using the real `torchmetrics.signal_noise_ratio`, not the fake unit-test metric.

Results:

`CASE 1: equal same-class counts`

Both versions selected the same assignment:

```text
raw assignment  ref_perm: [0, 1], est_perm: [1, 0]
SDRi assignment ref_perm: [0, 1], est_perm: [1, 0]
same assignment: True
mean SDRi: 30.7559
```

This confirms your point: when estimated/reference counts are equal, the baseline term is constant over permutations.

`CASE 2: one missing same-class estimate`

The two versions selected different reference subsets:

```text
raw assignment  ref_perm: [0], mean SDRi: -9.9147

same assignment: False
```

The comparison class reported:

```text
raw_sdr_assignment: -9.9147
sdri_assignment: 0.8892
delta_sdri_minus_raw: 10.8040
```

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-48-2026-04-26-10-20-51-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="48. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-48-2026-04-26-10-20-51-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll trace this from data generation through training targets, model outputs, S5 inference, and evaluation. The key question is whether the metric ever sees unequal same-class counts, not whether the separator tensors have fixed slot counts internally.

The first trace shows the condition is absolutely possible at evaluation: references and estimates are both fixed to 3 slots, but labels are counted after removing `silence`, so a `[dog, dog, silence]` reference versus `[dog, silence, silence]` prediction becomes exactly “one missing same-class estimate.” I’m checking whether the training objectives create or penalize that situation now.

The training data configs intentionally generate duplicate same-class events (`dupse_rate: 0.5`) and train with `n_sources: 3`, so reference-side `[dog, dog, silence]` is expected. I’m checking the actual extracted metadata split too, to see how often duplicate-label references occur in local data.

Yes, **case 2 is possible in the pipeline**, but mostly at **evaluation / S5 inference**, not as a structural tensor-shape issue during supervised separator training.

Training data can contain duplicate same-class references. The generated configs use `dupse_rate: 0.5`, and the local validation metadata confirms it:

```text
valid split parsed: 1800
zero target scenes: 300
duplicate-label scenes: 600 (33.3%)
examples:
  [&#x27;BicycleBell&#x27;, &#x27;Clapping&#x27;, &#x27;BicycleBell&#x27;]
  [&#x27;BicycleBell&#x27;, &#x27;BicycleBell&#x27;]
  [&#x27;Clapping&#x27;, &#x27;Clapping&#x27;]
```

So reference labels like:

```text
[&quot;dog&quot;, &quot;dog&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;]
```

are absolutely expected.

During TSE/USS supervised training, targets still have fixed `n_sources=3` slots. [TSEDataset](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/datamodules/tse_dataset.py:21) builds per-slot `label_vector` and `active_mask`, and [class_aware_pit_loss](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/training/loss/class_aware_pit.py:157) permits same-label swaps among active duplicate slots. So training does not “drop” the second dog structurally; it trains both active dog references.

But at S5 inference, labels come from the source classifier. In [Kwon2025S5._classify_sources](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/s5/kwo2025.py:54), every separated slot is classified independently. The classifier can output zero-vector silence via energy thresholding in [m2d_sc.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py:534). Then the evaluator counts non-silence labels per class in [s5capi_metric.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/evaluation/metrics/s5capi_metric.py:101).

So if reference is:

```text
[&quot;dog&quot;, &quot;dog&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;]
```

and S5 predicts:

```text
[&quot;dog&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;]
```

then metric-side class counts are:

```text
ref dog count = 2
est dog count = 1
```

That is exactly the crafted “one missing same-class estimate” case.

Important nuance: the model still outputs 3 waveform slots, but because the label for one slot is `silence` or a wrong class, the CAPI metric treats it as a false negative for the duplicated class. So yes, the case is possible and likely worth tracking on validation duplicate-label scenes. 019dc544-fe29-75c3-b814-651dfc4624c2" open><summary style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#dff5e7;color:#1c6b41;">ASSISTANT</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">48. <meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-50-2026-04-26-10-26-54-cst" data-role="assistant" data-label="50. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-50-2026-04-26-10-26-54-cst" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant Exactly. This is mainly a **system design / inference quality problem**, not a core metric-calculation bug.

The metric is doing what it should: if reference has two same-class sources but prediction only labels one as that class, then one source is effectively missed. The raw-vs-SDRi assignment variant only changes how that miss is paired/scored in an edge case; it does not solve the actual failure.

For TOP-1, the real target is to reduce case 2 frequency:

```text
ref: [&quot;dog&quot;, &quot;dog&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;]
est: [&quot;dog&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;]
```

or:

```text
ref: [&quot;dog&quot;, &quot;dog&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;]
est: [&quot;dog&quot;, &quot;cat&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;]
```

The fixes should be in the pipeline:

1. Better duplicate-source detection in SC
   Tune source classifier thresholds so a weak second same-class source is not suppressed as silence.

2. Per-slot silence calibration
   Measure false negative vs false positive tradeoff on zero-target and duplicate-label validation scenes separately.

3. Use USS/TSE energy/activity as extra evidence
   Do not rely only on SC class logits; combine waveform energy, temporal activity, and classifier confidence.

4. Duplicate-aware S5 refinement
   If USS produces two similar active foregrounds and SC labels one as `dog`, allow the second one to remain a `dog` candidate instead of forcing it to silence too aggressively.

5. Report duplicate-scene metrics separately
   Track CAPI-SDRi and label recall on scenes with same-class duplicates. That is where this failure will hide.

So I would keep the SDRi-assignment metric as a diagnostic comparison, but the main improvement work should go into **reducing missed duplicate same-class predictions**. 019dc544-fe29-75c3-b814-651dfc4624c2" open><summary style="border:1px solid #d7eadf;border-left:8px solid #3fa56b;background:#f5fcf7;border-radius:18px;padding:22px 24px;margin:14px 0 22px 0;box-shadow:0 6px 18px rgba(63,165,107,0.08);padding-bottom:14px;"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;"><span style="font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;padding:4px 10px;border-radius:999px;background:#dff5e7;color:#1c6b41;">ASSISTANT</span><span style="font-size:26px;font-weight:800;color:#172033;">50. <meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-52-2026-04-26-10-30-31-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="52. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-52-2026-04-26-10-30-31-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll turn this into an opt-in S5 inference improvement, not a destructive metric change. The likely path is to keep the classifier’s raw top class before silence thresholding, then let S5 recover high-confidence “silenced” slots as duplicate candidates when the waveform/activity evidence says they are real.

I’m going to keep this conservative: recover only silenced slots whose raw top class matches an already active predicted class in the same mixture, and whose confidence plus waveform energy clear thresholds. That targets duplicate misses without turning zero-target clips into broad false positives.

Next I’m wiring S5 to use those raw top classes only when explicitly enabled. The default stays old behavior, so existing configs keep the same false-positive/false-negative balance until we opt into the duplicate-recall mode.

The implementation is now opt-in via a sibling eval config, and the recipe explains how to run it. I’m running the focused tests and config parsing now; if anything shakes loose, I’ll tighten it before handing it back.

Implemented the duplicate-miss reduction as an **opt-in S5 inference mode**.

What changed:
  - `duplicate_recall_enabled`
  - `duplicate_recall_min_probability`
  - `duplicate_recall_min_waveform_rms`
- New eval config:
  [kwo2025_top1_like_lite_estimated_sc_duplicate_recall.yaml](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/evaluation/eval_configs/kwo2025_top1_like_lite_estimated_sc_duplicate_recall.yaml)

The rule is conservative: a silenced slot is recovered only if its raw top class matches an already active class in the same mixture and passes confidence + waveform RMS gates. So this targets:

```text
[&quot;dog&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;] -&gt; [&quot;dog&quot;, &quot;dog&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;]
```

without broadly turning silence into arbitrary labels.

Verification:
- `14 passed, 2 warnings`
- `py_compile` passed
- YAML check passed
- Crafted trace confirmed:
  - disabled: `[[&#x27;class_1&#x27;, &#x27;silence&#x27;, &#x27;silence&#x27;]]`
  - enabled: `[[&#x27;class_1&#x27;, &#x27;class_1&#x27;, &#x27;silence&#x27;]]`

<details id="msg-assistant-54-2026-04-26-10-36-42-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant I’ll check the actual configs and S5 variants rather than guessing from filenames. The improvement has two parts: SC exposing raw labels, and the S5 wrapper opting into using them.

Partly.

The SC-side change applies broadly to these source-classifier variants in [m2d_sc.py](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/m2dat/m2d_sc.py):

| Variant | Raw top-class output added? |
| --- | --- |
| `M2DSingleClassifier` | yes |
| `M2DSingleClassifierStrong` | yes |
| `M2DSingleClassifierTemporalStrong` | yes |
| `M2DPretrainedFusionClassifier` | yes, because it inherits `M2DSingleClassifierStrong.predict()` |

But the S5-side duplicate recovery only runs in [Kwon2025S5](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/src/models/s5/kwo2025.py), and only when:

```yaml
duplicate_recall_enabled: true
```

Currently only this new config enables it:

```text
src/evaluation/eval_configs/kwo2025_top1_like_lite_estimated_sc_duplicate_recall.yaml
```

So existing variants like these **can support it**, but do **not** currently enable it:

```text
kwo2025_top1_like_lite_strong_sc.yaml
kwo2025_top1_like_lite_beats_fusion_sc.yaml
kwo2025_top1_like_lite_fpasst_fusion_sc.yaml
kwo2025_top1_like_lite_uss.yaml
kwo2025_top1_like_chunked_uss.yaml
kwo2025_top1_like.yaml
```

It does **not** apply yet to:

Best next step: add sibling duplicate-recall eval configs for strong, BEATs-fusion, and fPaSST-fusion Kwon variants, so we can compare all of them without changing defaults.

<meta class="nav-message" data-anchor="msg-assistant-58-2026-04-26-10-44-12-cst-" data-role="assistant" data-label="58. Assistant" data-session="timeline">
<details id="msg-assistant-58-2026-04-26-10-44-12-cst-" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant Yes, and I think the right loss target is the source classifier’s silence decision, not the CAPI metric. I’ll trace what target context the SC loss currently receives, then add an opt-in duplicate-aware term that specifically increases recall for active sources whose class appears more than once in the mixture.

The current SC loss only sees `class_index`, `is_silence`, and optional span, so it cannot know whether an active source belongs to a duplicated class. I’m adding that target signal from the dataset first, then the loss can weight duplicated active sources more strongly against being silenced.

The loss I’m adding is deliberately narrow: it only activates for non-silence sources whose class appears at least twice in the same mixture, and it pushes their SC energy farther into the active region. That attacks the “second dog became silence” failure while leaving ordinary single-source and silence examples on the old loss unless the new lambda is set.

The data and loss plumbing is in. I’m adding tests for the new duplicate-class target and the loss gradient, then I’ll run the focused suite.

The new term is opt-in through `lambda_duplicate_recall`; with its default `0.0`, old configs behave the same. I’m adding the recipe note with the exact knobs, then running tests.

The compile check passed. The focused pytest is still running through the model smoke section; no failure output yet, so I’m waiting it out.

Yes. I added an opt-in SC training loss specifically for reducing Case 2.

What it does:
- `SourceClassifierDataset` now marks each source with:
  - `duplicate_class_count`
  - `is_duplicate_class`
  - `lambda_duplicate_recall`
  - `duplicate_m_in`

The new term only applies to active non-silence sources whose class appears more than once in the same mixture. It pushes their `energy` farther into the active region, so the classifier is less likely to threshold the second same-class source as silence.

Example config knobs:

```yaml
loss:
  module: src.training.loss.m2d_sc_arcface
  main: get_loss_func
  args:
    lambda_energy: 0.001
    m_in: -6.0
    m_out: -1.0
    lambda_duplicate_recall: 0.5
    duplicate_m_in: -8.0
```

I also documented this in [recipes.md](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/recipes.md).

Validation:
- `16 passed, 2 warnings`
- `py_compile` passed
- Crafted loss check:

So this is now ready to try in stage-2 SC training, where silence/energy thresholding is learned.

I added an opt-in SC training loss specifically for reducing Case 2.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">What it does:<br>- <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">SourceClassifierDataset</code> now marks each source with:<br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">duplicate_class_count</code><br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">is_duplicate_class</code><br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">lambda_duplicate_recall</code><br>  - <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">duplicate_m_in</code></p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">The new term only applies to active non-silence sources whose class appears more than once in the same mixture. It pushes their <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">energy</code> farther into the active region, so the classifier is less likely to threshold the second same-class source as silence.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Example config knobs:</p><div class="code-block" style="margin:10px 0 18px 0;border:1px solid #d6dce8;border-radius:14px;overflow:hidden;box-shadow:inset 0 1px 0 rgba(255,255,255,0.5);"><div style="display:flex;align-items:center;gap:10px;background:#1f2937;color:#e5edf7;font-size:12px;font-weight:800;letter-spacing:0.08em;text-transform:uppercase;padding:9px 12px;"><span>yaml</span><button class="copy-btn" type="button" onclick="copyCode(this)">Copy</button></div><pre style="margin:0;background:#0f1720;color:#e8eef6;padding:16px 18px;overflow:auto;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6;"><code>loss:
  module: src.training.loss.m2d_sc_arcface
  main: get_loss_func
  args:
    lambda_energy: 0.001
    m_in: -6.0
    m_out: -1.0
    lambda_duplicate_recall: 0.5
    duplicate_m_in: -8.0</code></pre></div><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">I also documented this in [recipes.md](/home/cmj/works/dcase2026/dcase2026_task4_baseline/recipes.md).</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">Validation:<br>- <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">16 passed, 2 warnings</code><br>- <code style="background:#eef3ff;color:#213b86;border:1px solid #cfdbff;border-radius:6px;padding:1px 6px;font-size:0.92em;font-family:SFMono-Regular,Consolas,'Liberation Mono',Menlo,monospace;">py_compile</code> passed<br>- Crafted loss check:</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">So this is now ready to try in stage-2 SC training, where silence/energy thresholding is learned.</p><p style="margin:0 0 14px 0;">&lt;oai-mem-citation&gt;<br>&lt;citation_entries&gt;<br>MEMORY.md:74-74|note=[CAPI-SDRi and silence suppression context]<br>MEMORY.md:110-110|note=[Kwon2025S5 relevance]<br>&lt;/citation_entries&gt;<br>&lt;rollout_ids&gt;<br>&lt;/rollout_ids&gt;<br>&lt;/oai-mem-citation&gt;</p></div></div></details>

<details id="msg-assistant-60-2026-04-26-10-49-22-cst" class="message-card" data-role="assistant" data-search="Assistant Current progress:

We clarified the CAPI metric issue. Equal same-class counts are fine because the mixture baseline is constant across permutations. The raw-SDR vs SDRi assignment difference only appears when prediction/reference counts differ for a class, such as:

```text
ref: [&quot;dog&quot;, &quot;dog&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;]
est: [&quot;dog&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;, &quot;silence&quot;]
```

To study that edge case, I added separate metric variants without changing the original metric:

Then we confirmed Case 2 is possible in this task/pipeline. The validation metadata has many duplicate-label scenes: 600/1800, about 33.3%. The issue is mostly model/inference design, not metric calculation.

